## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress response of a material as a function of strain and temperature, a fundamental constitutive relationship in solid mechanics where temperature modifies stiffness, hardening, and flow behavior.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime, small strains)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) (elastic modulus varying linearly with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic strain hardening)
- Ludwik hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (combined elastic and plastic response)
- Johnson-Cook simplified (no rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * (T**c4)) (hardening with power-law thermal term)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal activation effect on flow stress)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * (1 + c3 * T) (saturation hardening with thermal factor)
- Temperature-dependent power law: sigma = c0 * (epsilon**c1) * (T**c2) (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Arrhenius-Zener-Hollomon type: sigma = c0 * sinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (hyperbolic sine creep/flow model)
- Linear in both: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T (bilinear model with cross-term)
- Softening rational form: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * epsilon) * (1 + c2 * T) (saturating stress with thermal modulation)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal exponential)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening at high temperatures → multiplicative factor (1 - c*(T/Tm)**m) or exp(-c*T) reducing stress magnitude
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating dislocation density saturation
- Multiplicative decomposition of effects → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), separable strain hardening and thermal softening
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**n with 0 < n < 1 reflecting work hardening in metals
- Yield stress offset → additive constant c0 representing initial yield strength before hardening begins
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress → sinh(c*sigma) or inverse sinh appears in thermally-activated dislocation glide models
- Negative linear temperature dependence → elastic modulus and yield stress typically decrease linearly with T below melting
- Strain-temperature cross coupling → epsilon*T product terms capturing temperature-dependent hardening rate changes
- Phase transition discontinuities → abrupt changes in sigma-T relationship at critical temperatures suggesting structural transformations
- Exponential with reciprocal temperature → exp(c/T) indicating Arrhenius-type thermally activated deformation mechanisms
